# Lesson 1

<lesson>
	<title 'This is a book' - Introduction to simple statements and questions>
	<id 1>
	<level 4>
	<question objects 0.5>
		<concept this_is>
			<text This/That is...>
			<grammar DESU_SIMPLE1>
			<diagram diagram1>	
		</concept>
	</question>
	<question people 0.5>
		<concept person_is_1 0.5>
			<text [person] is...>
			<grammar DESU_SIMPLE1>
			<diagram diagram2>
		</concept>		
		<concept person_is_2 0.5>
			<text [person] is...>
			<grammar DESU_SIMPLE1>
			<diagram diagram2>
		</concept>
	</question>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Objects>
			question == objects
		</form_desc>		
		<form_desc People>
			question == people
		</form_desc>		
	</formgroup>	
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Statement>
			type == statement
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Question>
			type == question
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Positive>
			sign == positive 
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Negative>
			sign == negative
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Also>
			[Verb] == is_also
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>	
	# Default settings (only use if you want to restrict a certain form
	# Settings get passed to concept generation (included in concept, then resolved by grammar)
	<diagram diagram1>
		<gfxgroup>
			<gfx backdrop> 
				<coords 0 0 450 375>
				<image Backdrops/table-perspective.gif>
			</gfx>
		</gfxgroup>
		<gfxgroup>
			<gfx label>
				<text This>				
				<coords 50 15 325 28>				
				<restriction [Subject] == that>
					<sub This That>
				</restriction>
				<restriction {verbForm} type == statement>
					<appendS is>
				</restriction>
				<restriction [Verb] == is_also>
					<appendS also>
				</restriction>
				<restriction {verbForm} sign == negative>
					<appendS not>
				</restriction>	
				<restriction {verbForm} sign == positive>
					<appendS ...>
				</restriction>
				<restriction {verbForm} type == question>
					<insertS Is>
					<appendS ?>
					<sub This this>
					<sub That that>
				</restriction>
			</gfx>
		</gfxgroup>
		<gfxgroup>
			<gfx obj1> 
				<gfx_data [Complement]>			
				<coords 115 200 90 90>	
				<restriction [Subject] == that>
					<coords 250 200 90 90>	
				</restriction>
				<gfx_marker Misc/subject.gif>
				<gfx_marker_text This is the subject>
			</gfx>
			<gfx obj2> 
				<coords 250 200 90 90>
				<restriction [Subject] == that>
					<coords 115 200 90 90>	
				</restriction>
				<restriction [Verb] == is_also>
					<gfx_data [Complement]>
				</restriction>	
				<gfx_marker Misc/object.gif>
				<gfx_marker_text This is another object>				
			</gfx>
			<gfx misc1> 
				<coords 130 290 40 25>
				<text this>
				<image Misc/uparrow.gif>
				<restriction [Subject] == that>
					<text that>
					<coords 275 290 40 25>	
				</restriction>
			</gfx>
			<gfx negative>
				<restriction {verbForm} sign == negative>
					<text negative>
					<coords 160 290 25 25>
					<image Misc/negative.gif>				
				</restriction>
				<restriction [Subject] == that>
					<coords 305 290 25 25>	
				</restriction>
			</gfx>
		</gfxgroup>
	</diagram>
	<diagram diagram2 vcenter>
		<gfxgroup>
			<gfx obj1> 
				<gfx_data [Subject]>			
				<coords 50 110 150 150>	
				<gfx_marker Misc/subject.gif>
				<gfx_marker_text This is the subject>
			</gfx>
			<gfx obj2> 
				<gfx_data [Complement]>			
				<coords 250 110 150 150>	
				<gfx_marker Misc/info.gif>
				<gfx_marker_text Information about the subject>
			</gfx>
			<gfx negative>
				<restriction {verbForm} sign == negative>
					<text negative>
					<coords 350 210 50 50>
					<image Misc/negative.gif>				
				</restriction>
			</gfx>
			<gfx misc1>
				<text is>				
				<coords 175 275 100 20>
				<restriction [Verb] == is_also>
					<appendS also>
				</restriction>
				<restriction {verbForm} sign == negative>
					<appendS not>
				</restriction>
				<restriction {verbForm} sign == positive>
					<append ...>
				</restriction>
				<restriction {verbForm} type == question>
					<append ?>
				</restriction>
			</gfx>
		</gfxgroup>
	</diagram>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson1a.gif>
		<sentence Sally is not British>
		<answerJ サリーさん は イギリスじん ではありません >
		<answerK サリーさん は イギリス人 ではありません >
		<questionType Question Type - Questions about People>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Definitives
				<on>People
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Positive
				<on>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Also
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The Grammar Form shows us that we are talking about a person, and that the answer must 
			be a statement in the negative form. In this example, the concept of "also" is not used.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question you are asked to make a declarative statement or question about a person.
			Your answer may be a question about the person's nationality (for example, "Is Anne British?"), 
			or specify their job ("My brother is a doctor."). Please check the Grammar Form to 
			determine what form your response should be in.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			We can see that Sally is the subject (marked with S), and that we
			are being asked to comment on whether she is British (information,
			marked with I).  In this case she is not, as is indicated by the cross in
			the diagram.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson1b.gif>
		<sentence Is this a map?>
		<answerJ これ は ちず ですか >
		<answerK これ は 地図 ですか >
		<questionType Question Type - Questions about Objects with Definitives>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Definitives
				<off>People
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Statement
				<on>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Also
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to ask a 
			question about an object using a definitive (this, that, etc).
			The question should be in the positive form. The concept of "also"
			is not used in this case.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You are sitting at a table opposite your friend.  If the object
			is closer to you, i.e. in the lower half of the table, it is refered 
			to as "this".  For example, "This is a pen". If it is closer to your friend, you should refer to it as "that".  
			For example, "Is that a bag?". When two objects are shown which are the same, your description of the
			selected object should include the word "also".  For example, "Is that also a CD?".
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The object, a map, is closer to you and thus addressed as "This". 
			You are asked to form a question, and the question you would be
			expected to ask (in Japanese) is, "Is this a map?"
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson1c.gif>
		<sentence That is also a hamburger>
		<answerJ それ も ハンバーガー です>
		<answerK それ も ハンバーガー です>
		<questionType Statements about Objects with Definitives>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Definitives
				<off>People
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Also
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to give a
			statement about an object using a definitive (this, that, etc).
			The statement should be in the positive form. We must use the word
			"also" in our answer.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You are sitting at a table opposite your friend.  If the object
			is closer to you, i.e. on your side of the table, it is referred
			to as "this".  For example, "This is a pen". If it is closer to your friend, you should refer to it as "that".  
			For example, "Is that a bag?". When two objects are shown which are the same, your description of the
			selected object should include the word "also".  For example, "Is that also a CD?".
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			There are two objects, but the focus is on the one further from
			you, so you should refer to it as "that". As there are two identical objects,
			you must use the word "also" in your answer,  i.e. "That is also..."
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
</lesson>

<lesson>

	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson2a.gif>
		<sentence I will read a magazine at home>
		<answerJ わたし は うち で ざっし を よみます>
		<answerK 私 は 家 で 雑誌 を 読みます>
		<questionType Question Type - Simple Statements>
		<form>		
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>	
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to give a
			statement about an action.  This should be a positive statement
			using the non-past tense.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You are asked to describe an action, or construct a question about an action.
			The diagram may contain information on who did the action, where they did it,
			when it was carried out, what the object was, etc.  All displayed information
			should be given in your answer.  Extra information should not be included.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The subject (S) is you. The place (P) is your home.  The object of the
			action (O) is a magazine.  The action itself, i.e. the verb (V) is To Read.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson2b.gif>
		<sentence I did not go to the bank with my grandmother>
		<answerJ わたし は おばあさん と ぎんこう へ いきませんでした>
		<answerK 私 は おばあさん と 銀行 へ 行きませんでした>
		<questionType Question Type - Simple Statements>
		<form>		
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Positive
				<on>Negative
			</fgroup>	
			<fgroup>
				<off>Non-Past
				<on>Past
			</fgroup>	
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to give a
			statement about an action.  This should be a negative statement,
			using the past tense.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You are asked to describe an action, or construct a question about an action.
			The diagram may contain information on who did the action, where they did it,
			when it was carried out, what the object was, etc.  All displayed information
			should be given in your answer.  Extra information should not be included.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The subject (S) is you. The action was performed with (+) your grandmother.
			The place (P) is the bank.  The action itself, i.e. the verb (V) is "to go," but is
			in the negative form.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson2c.gif>
		<sentence Will you read the book?>
		<answerJ ほん を よみますか>
		<answerK 本 を 読みますか>
		<questionType Question Type - Simple Questions>
		<form>		
			<fgroup>
				<off>Statement
				<on>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to ask a
			question about an possible action.  This should be a positive question,  
			and the non-past tense should be used.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You are asked to describe an action, or construct a question about an action.
			The diagram may contain information on who did the action, where they did it,
			when it was carried out, what the object was, etc.  All displayed information
			should be given in your answer.  Extra information should not be included.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The object (O) that the action relates to is a book.
			The action itself, i.e. the verb (V) is "to read," and should
			be given as a question.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
</lesson>

# Lesson 3
#
#####################################################################
<lesson>
	<title 'Describing location' - Introduction to relative locations>
	<id 3>
	<level 4>
	<question inanimate 0.9>
		<concept position_in_room1 0.1>
			<grammar Rel_Position>
			<diagram diagram1>
		</concept>
		<concept position_in_room2 0.9>
			<grammar Rel_Position>
			<diagram diagram2>
		</concept>
	</question>
	<question animate 0.1>
		<concept person_position 1.0>
			<grammar person_position>
			<diagram diagram3>
		</concept>
	</question>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Animate>
			question == animate
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Inanimate>
			question == inanimate
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Location>
			question != ownership
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Ownership>
			question == ownership
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Positive>
			sign == positive 
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Negative>
			sign == negative
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Statement>
			type == statement
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Question>
			type == question
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>
	<diagram diagram1>
		<gfxgroup>
			<gfx backdrop> 
				<coords 0 0 450 375>
				<image Backdrops/room1.gif>
			</gfx>
			<gfx tv>
				<coords 165 30 50 60>
				<image INVISIBLE>
				<text Clock>
			</gfx>
			<gfx tv>
				<coords 10 60 137 188>
				<image INVISIBLE>
				<text Shelves>
			</gfx>
			<gfx tv>
				<coords 82 256 240 87>
				<image INVISIBLE>
				<text Bed>
			</gfx>
			<gfx tv>
				<coords 375 210 75 165>
				<image INVISIBLE>
				<text Drawers>
			</gfx>
		</gfxgroup>
		<gfxgroup>
			<gfx subject> 
				<gfx_data [Subject]>			
				<coords 325 18 75 75>	
			</gfx>
		</gfxgroup>
		<gfxgroup>
			<gfx location> 
				<restriction [Where] == on_bed>
					<text It's here!>
					<coords 205 245 40 40>
					<image Misc/here.gif>				
				</restriction>
				<restriction [Where] == under_bed>
					<text It's here!>
					<coords 205 342 40 40>
					<image Misc/here.gif>				
				</restriction>
				<restriction [Where] == on_shelf>
					<text It's here!>
					<coords 70 50 40 40>
					<image Misc/here.gif>				
				</restriction>
				<restriction [Where] == on_drawer>
					<text It's here!>
					<coords 410 180 40 40>

	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson3a.gif>
		<sentence The pencil was under the bed>
		<answerJ えんぴつ は ベッド の した に ありました>
		<answerK 鉛筆 は ベッド の 下 に ありました>
		<questionType Question Type - Relative Location of an Item>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Non-past
				<on>Past
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to give a
			statement about the location of an object. This statement should be positive,
			using past tense.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You can see a picture of a room, and are asked either to explain or
			ask the whereabouts of an object in the room.  The object is shown
			in the top-right of the diagram.  A location in the room is marked by a green tick or a red cross,
			depending on whether the object is at that location. The location should always be expressed 
			with regards to another object (such as next to the TV, or under the bed, etc).
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The object in question is a pencil (shown top-right).  The location as marked
			by the green tick is under the bed.  If the marker
			was a red cross, it would show that the object was not at the highlighted location.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson3b.gif>
		<sentence The computer is not next to the TV>
		<answerJ パソコン は テレビ の となり に ありません>
		<answerK パソコン は テレビ の となり に ありません>
		<questionType Question Type - Relative Location of an Item>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Positive
				<on>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to give a
			statement about the location of an object. This statement should be negative,
			using the non-past tense.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You can see a picture of a room, and are asked either to explain or
			ask the whereabouts of an object in the room.  The object is shown
			in the top-right of the diagram.  A location in the room is marked by a green tick or a red cross,
			depending on whether the object is at that location. The location should always be expressed 
			with regards to another object (such as next to the TV, or under the bed, etc).
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The object in question is a personal computer (shown top-right).  The location marked
			by the cross is next to (or to the left of) the television. 
			In this case the cross is red which shows the object is not at that location.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson3c.gif>
		<sentence Mother is at home>
		<answerJ はは は うち に います>
		<answerK 母 は 家 に います>
		<questionType Question Type - Location of a Person>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to give a
			statement about the location of a person. This statement should be positive,
			and the non-past tense should be used.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You are shown the picture of a person, the subject (S) of the sentence.  You will also
			be shown a place (P).  This is the place where the person may or may not be (depending
			on the desired form of the answer).  The word below these two images gives a clue
			as to the desired form, whether the person is or isn't at the shown location, etc.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The subject (S) in this case is your mother.  The place (P) that we are considering is your home.  
			The word "is" is a guide to show that your mother is at home (thus a positive sentence).
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
</lesson>

		<diagram Examples/lesson4_1.png>
		<sentence That hamburger is hot>
		<answerJ その ハンバーガー は あつい です>
		<answerK その ハンバーガー は 熱い です>
		<questionType Question Type - Standard Adjectives>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Standard
				<off>Modifier
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Also
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to give a
			statement, using an adjective to describe the object.  
			This statement should be positive.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You are sitting at a table opposite your friend.  If the object
			is closer to you, i.e. on your side of the table, it should be referred to as "this," 
			If it is closer to your friend, it should be referred to as "that." If the grammar
			form indicates the concept "Also" is used, then you should include 
			the word "also" in your answer. Further information about the object (in other words,
			the adjective(s) you should use) is given in the blue box.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The subject (S) is a hamburger, and because there is a demonstrative (D), 
			it should be referred to as "that hamburger". 
			The description of the object is that it is hot.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson4_2.png>
		<sentence This is a cheap and delicious apple>
		<answerJ これ は やすくて おいしい りんご です>
		<answerK これ は 安くて おいしい りんご です>
		<questionType Question Type - Adjectives that Modify Nouns>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Standard
				<on>Modifier
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Also
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to give a
			statement, using a modifying adjective to describe the object.  
			This statement should be positive.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You are sitting at a table opposite your friend.  If the object
			is closer to you, i.e. in the lower half of the table, it is refered 
			to as "This". If it is closer to your friend, you should refer to it as "That".  
			When two objects are shown which are the same, your description of the
			selected object should include the meaning "also". Further information about the object (in other words,
			the adjective(s) you should use) is given in the blue box.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The object is an apple, and as it is near you, thus is referred to as "this". 
			The description of the object is that it is both cheap and delicious.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
</lesson>

	</diagram>

			The non-past tense should be used.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You are asked to suggest a course of action.
			The diagram may contain information on what action is to be carried out, the place (marked with P)
			it will be carried out, how it will be done (marked with H), with whom, etc.  All displayed information
			should be given in your answer.  Extra information should not be included.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			From the text at the top of the diagram, we can see that the answer should be a suggestion.
			The object (O) of the suggested action is coffee.  The action itself, 
			i.e. the verb (V) is "to drink."
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

			The non-past tense should be used.
		</formHelp>

			You are asked to invite someone to partake in a course of action with you.
			The diagram may contain information on what action is to be carried out, where
			it will be carried out, etc.  All displayed information
			should be given in your answer.  Extra information should not be included.
		</gfxHelp>

			The object (O) of the suggested action is cake.

		</diagHelp>

		<form>

				<off>Forbidden
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Statement
				<on>Question
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we must make a request for permission to perform
			an action, and that the answer must be a question.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This form of question requires you to ask permission to perform an action. Because
			the subject of the sentence is yourself, it is omitted in the answer.
			The diagram shows the details of the action that you are asking permission to do,
			such as the direct object and the verb to use.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The text at the top of the diagram shows us the basic form of the answer ("Is is OK to ... ?").
			In this case, the verb (V) is "to eat" and the direct object (O) is bread.
			So we must ask permission to eat some bread.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

		<form>

				<off>Permission
				<on>Forbidden
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows that we must forbid an action, and that our answer needs to be a statement.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This type of question requires you to forbid someone to perform the action shown
			in the diagram. You are speaking directly to the subject, and do not need to explicitly
			include it in the answer. The diagram shows both the verb of the action to forbid and its direct object.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			From the diagram, we can see that the verb (V) is smoking and the object (O) is a cigarette.
			So the answer is a request forbidding the listener from smoking cigarettes.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

			an action because the "positive" and "statement" forms are active. We must use the non-past
			plain form of the verb.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This type of question requires you to give a reason with "kara" for performing (or not performing)
			an action. The diagram shows the basic structure of the sentence with English words,
			and uses pictures for the details, such as the reason, the verb (V)
			describing the action, the direct object (O) of the verb, or the time
			(T) at which the action is performed.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The adjective indicated with a green "Aj" box is "hot." This picture occurs before 
			the word "then," so it is the reason for action described in the second part of the answer.
			The verb (V) is "to drink" and the direct object (O) is cola.
		</diagHelp>

		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This type of question is similar to the one in the first example because you must give a
			reason for performing (or not performing) an action, except in this case the reason is given with
			"Node" instead of "Kara." The reason may be a time (T), such as a specific day, or a subordinate
			clause. The diagram shows the basic structure of the sentence with English words,
			and uses pictures for the details, such as the reason, the verb (V)
			describing the action, the direct object (O) of the verb, or the time
			(T) at which the action is performed, etc.
		</gfxHelp>

			action. The verb (V) describing the action is "to go" and the direct object (O) is a church, so the
			activity is "going to church."
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson9_3.png>
		<sentence Taro's bag is heavy.>
		<answerJ たろう の かばん は おもい ん です>
		<answerK 太郎 の 鞄 は 重い ん です>
		<questionType Question Type - Explanations>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>"から"
				<off>"なので/ので"
				<on>"ん-だ/ん-です"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that the answer
			should be a positive statement in the form of an explanation using
			"N-da/N-desu," and that we must use the non-past polite form of the copula.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This type of lesson requires you to give an explanation using "N-da" or "N-desu." In the diagram
			you are shown an object, the object's owner, and an adjective which describes some
			property of the object. Your answer should describe the object with
			the adjective and "N-da" or "N-desu" as specified in the grammar form.
			All displayed information should be given in your answer, and extra information should not be included.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			In the diagram, the owner (S) is shown above the
			object (S) that he or she owns. The adjective (Aj) that describes the
			object is shown on the right side.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
</lesson>

		<diagram Examples/lesson12_1.png>
		<sentence Sally hasn't eaten lunch yet>
		<answerJ サリーは まだ ちゅうしょくを たべて いません>
		<answerK サリーは まだ 昼食を 食べて いません>
		<questionType Question Type - Not yet>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>"まだ"
				<off>"もう"
				<off>"までに"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Positive
				<on>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we must make a statement using "Mada" and the negative form of a verb.
			The answer must also be in the non-past polite form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question you will practise expressing that an action has not yet been performed or that
			something has not happened yet. The key idea is that some state has not changed between some time
			in the past and the time your answer is said. The subject who performs the action and the
			associated verb are shown in the diagram, and the direct object of the verb may also be shown.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The diagram indicates that the subject (S) is Sally, the verb is "to eat," and the direct 
			object (O) is "lunch." The main concept "still/yet" is shown with a green box marked "Av."
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson12_2.png>
		<sentence Sally has already finished reading the book>

		<questionType Question Type - Already>

			<fgroup>

				<off>"までに"
			</fgroup>

				<off>Question
			</fgroup>

				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>

				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Polite
				<off>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			From the grammar form, we can see that the
			answer must be a positive statement using "Mou," and that the verb
			should be in the non-past polite form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question you are asked to express that an action has
			been completed, or that a change in state has occurred. For positive
			sentences the nuance is 'already,' while for negative ones it is 'no
			longer' or 'not anymore.' The diagram shows the subject who performs
			the action, the verb expressing the action, and the direct object of
			the verb. However, if no verb is given you must use "iru" in your answer.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The diagram indicates that the subject (S) is Sally, the verb is "to read," and the direct 
			object (O) is a book. The main concept, "already," is marked with a green box marked "Av."
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

			statement using "Madeni," and also that the verb must be in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>

			For this type of question, you must express
			that an action was (or will be) completed by a certain time. The diagram shows
			the verb that expresses the action, the direct object, the time
			specifying when the action will be completed by, and also English
			words which show the structure of the answer.

<lesson>
	<title 'I want to go to Kyoto' - Intentions and desires>
	<id 14>
	<level 4>
	<level 3>
	<question hoshii 1.0>
		<concept lesson14-3 1.0>
			<grammar lesson14-3>
			<diagram lesson14-3>
		</concept>
	</question>
	<question shitehoshi 1.0>
		<concept lesson14-4 1.0>
			<grammar lesson14-4>
			<diagram lesson14-4>
		</concept>
	</question>
	<question tai 1.0>
		<concept lesson14-1 1.0>
			<grammar lesson14-1>
			<diagram lesson14-1>
		</concept>
	</question>
	<question tsumorida 1.0>
		<concept lesson14-2 1.0>
			<grammar lesson14-2>
			<diagram lesson14-2>
		</concept>
	</question>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc WantToDo>
			question == tai
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc PlanToDo>
			question == tsumorida
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Want>
			question == hoshii
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc WantSomeoneToDo>
			question == shitehoshi
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>

		<sentence I want to go to Kyoto>
		<answerJ わたしは きょうとに いき たい>
		<answerK 私は 京都に 行き たい>
		<questionType Question Type - Your Own Desires>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>WantToDo
				<off>PlanToDo
				<off>Want
				<off>WantSomeoneToDo
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows that you must express
			your own desire to perform an action with the "tai" form,
			and that your answer should be in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question, you are asked to
			express your own strong desire to perform a specified action, using the
			"tai" form of the indicated verb. Because you can only use this form
			when talking about your own desire or intention, the subject will
			always be yourself. The diagram indicates the type of
			answer you should give, as well as the verb describing the action and
			details such as the direct object.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The diagram indicates that the subject (S) is
			yourself, the action is the verb (V) "to go," and that the direct
			object is "Kyoto." There are also some English words to show you the
			basic structure of the answer you need to give.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

				<off>Plain

			your plan to perform an action using "tsumori,"
			and that your answer should be in the polite past form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This type of question requires you to indicate
			some person's plans or intention to perform an action using "tsumori."
			Because this construct can be used for both your own plans or the
			plans of others, you need to pay attention to the subject shown in
			the diagram. The diagram also shows which verb to use when describing
			the action and details such as the direct object. You should include
			all relevant details in your answer.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The diagram indicates that the subject (S) is
			yourself, the action is the verb (V) "to return," and that the direct
			object is "university." There are also some English words to show you the
			basic structure of your answer.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

		<diagram Examples/lesson14_3.png>
		<sentence I want some cold coffee>

		<answerK 私 は 冷たい コーヒー が 欲しい です>
		<questionType Question Type - Desire for Objects>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>WantToDo
				<off>PlanToDo
				<on>Want
				<off>WantSomeoneToDo
			</fgroup>

				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Polite
				<off>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows that you must express
			some person's desire for the object shown using "hoshii,"
			and that your answer should be in the non-past polite form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question, you will practise
			indicating desire for an object with the adjective "hoshii." The
			diagram indicates the subject of the sentence, as well as the object
			that is wanted and details such as an adjective describing the object.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The diagram indicates that the subject (S) is
			yourself and that the object is "coffee"
			described by the adjective (Aj) "cold." It
			also shows that you will use the adjective (Aj) "hoshii"
			to show that you want it.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

		<diagram Examples/lesson14_4.png>
		<sentence I don't want Sam to go back to Britain>
		<answerJ わたしは サムに イギリスに かえって ほしくない>
		<answerK 私は サムに イギリスに 帰って 欲しくない>
		<questionType Question Type - Desire for Others' Actions>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>WantToDo
				<off>PlanToDo
				<off>Want
				<on>WantSomeoneToDo
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Positive
				<on>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			You are required to express desire for someone
			not to perform an action, using "hoshii."
			Your answer should be in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			You are asked to express your desire for
			someone else to perform an action using the adjective "hoshii." The
			top half of the diagram shows the subject of the sentence and the
			object, which is the person who performs the
			action that the subject is commenting on.
			The bottom half of the diagram describes that action with a verb and
			may also include a direct object.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The top half of the diagram shows the subject
			(S), yourself, and the object (O), Sam, whose action you are
			commenting on. Sam's action is described by verb "to
			go" and the direct object (O) "Britain."
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows that you must use "Tari"
			to list actions in a positive statement, and that your answer should
			be in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			For this type of question, you must list two
			actions out of a larger list using the "Tari" form of the associated verbs. The diagram
			shows the verbs and direct objects of both actions. When giving your
			answer, the action in the top half of the diagram should be given
			before the one in the bottom half.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			From the diagram, we can see that the verb in
			both cases is "to drink." The object (O) is cola in the first case
			and orange juice in the second.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson15_2.png>
		<sentence Sometimes I see it on TV and sometimes I hear about it from others>
		<answerJ テレビ で みたり ひと から きいたり する>
		<answerK テレビ で 見たり 人 から 聞いたり する>

		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>"たり"
				<off>"や"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The answer must use the "Tari" form of the
			verbs to make a positive statement in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question, you will practise
			expressing alternating actions using the "Tari" form of
			verbs. While the first example used "Tari" to give a few examples of
			actions out of a longer list, in this case the nuance is that
			sometimes one action is performed and sometimes the other one is.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The diagram shows that the verb (V) describing
			the first action is "to see" and that the object (O) is
			"TV," while the verb for second action is "to ask."
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson15_3.png>
		<sentence I drank cola, orange juice, and other things>
		<answerJ コーラ や オレンジジュース を のみました>
		<answerK コーラ や オレンジジュース を 飲みました>
		<questionType Question Type - Listing Nouns>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>"たり"
				<on>"や"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Non-Past
				<on>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The answer must use "Ya" to list nouns, and
			should be a positive statement in the polite past form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This type of question requires you to give an
			incomplete list of nouns by using "Ya." Unlike "To," which is used to
			when giving complete lists of things, "Ya" implies that you are
			giving the two nouns shown in the diagram as examples without
			mentioning the rest of the items in the list.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The verb (V) is "to drink" and the direct objects (O) are cola and orange juice.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
</lesson>

	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson16_1.png>
		<sentence If we are busy, we won't go to the theater.>
		<answerJ もし いそがしい なら えいがかん に いかない>
		<answerK もし 忙しい なら 映画館 に 行かない>
		<questionType Question Type - Conditional Statements ('Nara')>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>"なら"
				<off>"と"
				<off>"たら"
				<off>"ば"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Positive
				<on>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we must
			use 'Nara' for the condition, and that the result is a negative statement in the non-past tense.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This question type asks you to form a
			conditional sentence using 'Nara,' which is somewhat similar to the
			construct 'if .. then' in English. The top half of the diagram shows the condition corresponding
			to 'if' and the bottom half shows the result (or main sentence) described with 'then,' which holds
			only if the condition is true. All displayed information should be given in your answer, and
			extra information should not be included.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The English words in the diagram indicate the
			basic structure of the answer. The condition for "if" is the
			adjective (Aj) "busy," and the verb (V) "to go" along with its direct
			object (O) theater is the result for "then."
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson16_2.png>
		<sentence When summer comes, it become hot.>
		<answerJ なつに なる と あつく なる>
		<answerK 夏に なる と 暑く なる>
		<questionType Question Type - Natural Consequences ('To')>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>"なら"
				<on>"と"
				<off>"たら"
				<off>"ば"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that the answer must
			use 'To' to indicate the condition, and the positive non-past form of the verb in the result.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			For this type of question, you must use 'To' to
			indicate that something happens as a natural consequence of a
			given condition. This type of sentence is only used when the result
			is uncontrollable and certain to occur (or when the speaker is
			convinced that this is so). The top half of the diagram shows the condition, and the bottom half
			shows the result.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			In the condition the subject (S) is summer and
			the verb (V) is "to become," and the result is the adjective (Aj) hot
			followed by the verb (V) "to become."
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson16_3.png>
		<sentence If it rains, I won't go to the library>
		<answerJ もし あめ が ふっ たら としょかん に いかない>
		<answerK もし 雨 が 降っ たら 図書館 に 行かない>
		<questionType Question Type - General Conditionals ('Tara')>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>"なら"
				<off>"と"
				<on>"たら"
				<off>"ば"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Positive
				<on>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that the answer must use the 'Tara' form
			of the verb for the condition, and the negative non-past form of the verb in the result.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question, you are asked to
			give a simple conditional statement using the 'Tara' form of the verb. While this
			construct is similar to 'Nara' that was introduced in the first
			example, 'Tara' can be used for more general kinds of conditional
			statements where the emphasis is placed on the result. As before, the top half
			of the diagram shows the condition and the bottom half shows the result.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The diagram uses English words to indicate the
			condition, which is "if it rains" in this case. The result is the
			action described by the verb (V) "to go" and the direct object (O) library.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson16_4.png>
		<sentence If Sally comes, we can play volleyball.>
		<answerJ サリー が くれ ば バレーボール が できる>
		<answerK サリー が 来れ ば バレーボール が 出来る>
		<questionType Question Type - General Conditionals ('Ba')>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>"なら"
				<off>"と"
				<off>"たら"
				<on>"ば"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that the answer must use the 'Ba' form of the
			verb for the condition, and that the result must use the positive non-past form of the verb.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			For this type of question, you are asked to 
			set a condition on a sentence using the 'Ba' form of the verb. A
			conditional statement of this type has a more objective nuance, and
			cannot be used when the result describes the speaker's volitional
			actions. As in the other examples, the top half of the diagram describes the
			condition and the bottom half shows the result.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			We can see that the subject (S) of the
			condition is Sally, and that the verb is "to come." In the result,
			the object (O) is playing volleyball.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we need to use
			the 'Must' pattern, and that the answer should be in the non-past
			plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			For this type of question, you must express an
			obligation to perform an action using the negative 'ba' form of a
			verb plus the verb 'naru.' The diagram shows the verb describing the
			action and details such as its direct object and the time when the
			action will be performed.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The English text at the top of the diagram
			shows the basic structure of the answer. We can see that the verb (V)
			describing the action is "to go" and that the direct object (O) is
			school. The time (T) that the action will be performed is tomorrow.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson17_3.png>
		<sentence It is better to ask to Sally about Mathematics.>
		<answerJ すうがく の こと なら サリー に きいたら いい>
		<answerK 数学 の こと なら サリー に 聞いたら いい>
		<questionType Question Type - Suggestions>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>HadBetter
				<off>Must
				<on>It'sBetterTo
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that the answer must be a suggestion in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question you will practise an expression used for suggesting that someone
			ask another person for advice on a particular topic. In this case, the verb is "to ask," so the
			diagram shows the person to ask (marked as a direct object) and the topic being discussed.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The English text shows the basic structure of
			the answer. We can see that the direct object
			(O) of "to ask" is Sally and the topic to ask
			her about is Mathematics.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
</lesson>

		<sentence Before I go to the barbershop, I drink some tea.>
		<answerJ とこや に いく まえ に おちゃ を のんだ>
		<answerK 床屋 に 行く 前 に お茶 を 飲んだ>
		<questionType Question Type - Before and After>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Before
				<off>After
				<off>Then
				<off>While
				<off>During
				<off>Flequency
				<off>By
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Non-Past
				<on>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			In this case, 'Before' will be used, though 'After' is also possible for this
			question type. The answer should be a positive statement in the past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question, you are asked to
			give a simple ordering of events, expressing the fact that one takes
			place before or after the other. The bottom half of the diagram shows the main action, while
			the top half shows the preposition and event that are used to describe
			when the main action was performed. Your answer should use the
			appropriate preposition, either 'mae ni' (before) or 'ato de' (after), along with the correct form of
			the verb shown in the top half of the diagram.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			verb "to go" and the direct object (O) barbershop. The main action is described
			by the verb (V) "to drink" and the direct object (O) tea.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

			In this type of question, you will practise
			combining two sentences with the 'te' form and indicating that the
			action described in one occurs before the other one. This grammar
			pattern is similar to 'ato de' (covered in the first example), but
			implies that the first action was completed before the second one
			begins. The top half of the diagram shows the first action, while the
			bottom half shows the second one.

			expression 'aida ni,' which is used when a speaker emphasizes that an

			the 'Frequency' pattern, and that the answer must be a positive
			statement in the non-past polite form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This type of question requires you to express
			that a regularly occurring or habitual action is performed a certain number of times within a
			given time period. The top half of the diagram shows the time period
			and the action's frequency, while the bottom half describes the
			action by listing the subject, verb, and details such as the object
			of the verb. 
		</gfxHelp>

			period (T), one month, and the frequency of the action, three

			For this question type, you must express that
			the action shown in the diagram is expected to be completed by a
			certain time by using 'made ni.' The time period indicates the latest
			possible time at which the action can complete. The diagram shows the
			time period in the top half and the action in the bottom half.
		</gfxHelp>

<lesson>
	<title 'I will try this' - Intentional actions>
	<id 19>
	<level 3>
	<question mitai 1.0>
		<concept lesson19-1 1.0>
			<grammar lesson19-1>
			<diagram lesson19-1>
		</concept>
		<concept lesson19-2 1.0>
			<grammar lesson19-2>
			<diagram lesson19-2>
		</concept>

		<sentence Just once, I'd like to try going to America>
		<answerJ あめりか に いちど いってみたい>
		<answerK アメリカ に 一度 行ってみたい>
		<questionType Question Type - Trying Something Out>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>DesireToTry
				<off>Preparation
				<off>Completion
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form indicates that your answer
			must use 'Mitai,' and that it should be a positive statement in the
			non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question, you are asked to
			practice expressing desire to try doing something. Your answer will
			make use of the verb 'miru,' which can be added after the 'te' form
			of a verb to express the concept of trying something out. The diagram
			shows the details of the action, such as the verb used and the place
			where it is performed.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The English text at the top of the diagram
			shows the basic structure of the answer. The action is described by
			the verb (V) "to go," specifically to the place (P), America. The adverb (Av) once
			gives additional information about the action.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

			express that an action was done in preparation for something or for
			future convenience. This can be expressed by adding the verb 'Oku' to

			was performed to completion. This grammar
			pattern can also show that the speaker views the results of the
			action as regrettable. The diagram shows the verb used to describe the action as well as its
			direct object. All displayed information should be given in your answer, and extra information should not be included.
		</gfxHelp>

			action is "to drink," and that the direct object (O) is beer.

				<off>"ようだ/です"

				<on>Plain

			should use the 'SouDa/Desu' pattern, and should be a positive
			statement in the non-past plain form.:endfh:
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question you will practice
			giving your impression of a situation with an adjective and 'sou
			da/desu.' This construct is used when the speaker is describing how something
			appears or making a guess about it, using direct evidence from their
			own perceptions. The diagram shows the subject to describe and the
			adjective to use for the description.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The diagram shows that the subject (S) is
			Imanishi and the adjective (Aj) describing her is busy. The English
			text gives the basic structure of the answer.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson20_2.png>

		<answerK サリーさんは美術館に行くはずです>
		<questionType Question Type - Expectations>
		<form>
			<fgroup>

				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>

				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>

			The grammar form shows us that the answer
			should use the 'HazuDa/Desu' pattern, and should be a positive
			statement in the non-past polite form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question, you are asked to
			express an expectation using 'Hazu da/desu' about the outcome of an
			event based on available evidence. This grammar pattern is used to
			express what the speaker expects as the natural result given the
			available facts. The diagram shows the action to be commented on,
			including the subject, verb, and details such as the direct object.
		</gfxHelp>

			The diagram shows that the subject (S) is
			Sally and that the verb (V) expressing the action is
			"to go" with a museum as its direct object. The English text marked with (P) shows us
			that this is probably going to happen according to the speaker.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson20_3.png>
		<sentence Michiko seems like a student>
		<answerJ みちこは がくせい みたい です>
		<answerK 道子は 学生 みたい です>
		<questionType Question Type - Conclusions based on Appearances>
		<form>
			<fgroup>

				<off>Past
			</fgroup>

				<off>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			In this case we use the 'MitaiDa/Desu'
			pattern, though the 'YouDa/Desu' pattern is also possible for this
			type of question. The answer should be a positive statement in the non-past polite form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This type of question asks you practise saying that one
			thing seems like something else, or appears to have some quality. The
			answer should use either the grammar pattern 'mitai da/desu' or
			conclusion, but these grammar patterns imply that the speaker has
			considered other information or spent some time reasoning about the
			situation. The diagram shows the subject to be commented on.
		</gfxHelp>

			basic form that the answer should take. We can see that the subject
			(S) is Michiko and the object (O) that she resembles is a student.

	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson20_4.png>
		<sentence It will probably be sunny tomorrow>

				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>

				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>

			should use 'Darou/Deshou,' and also that it should be a positive
			statement in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question you will practice
			making conjectures with 'darou' and 'deshou.' These grammar patterns
			show that the speaker is reasonably sure of the outcome of an unknown
			event (not volitional actions) based on the available facts. The diagram shows the event that is to be commented on.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The English text in the diagram shows the
			basic form that the answer should take. The diagram indicates that the time (T) tomorrow
			is supposed to be described as sunny using the verb (V) "is."

	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson20_5.png>
		<sentence Sally might play soccer>
		<answerJ サリーさん は サッカー を する かもしれない>
		<answerK サリーさん は サッカー を する かもしれない>
		<questionType Question Type - Expressing Possibilities>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>"そうだ/です"
				<off>"はずだ/です"

				<off>"みたいだ/です"

				<off>"か-どうか"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form indicates that the answer
			should use 'KamoShirenai,' and also that it should be a positive
			statement in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question, you are asked to
			express that an event is possible but not likely using the grammar
			pattern 'ka mo shirenai.' The diagram shows the details of the event,
			such as the subject who performs it and the verb describing the action.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The English text in the diagram shows the
			basic form that the answer should take. The
			diagram indicates that Sally is the subject (S) and that soccer is
			the object (O).
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson20_6.png>
		<sentence I can't tell whether this orange juice is delicious or not>
		<answerJ この オレンジジュース は おいしい かどうか わからない>
		<answerK この オレンジジュース は おいしい かどうか わからない>
		<questionType Question Type - Whether>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>"そうだ/です"
				<off>"はずだ/です"
				<off>"ようだ/です"
				<off>"みたいだ/です"
				<off>"だろう/でしょう"
				<off>"かも-しれない"
				<on>"か-どうか"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form indicates that the answer
			should use 'KaDouka,' and also that it should be a positive
			statement in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			For this type of question, you must express
			that you can't tell whether something is the case or not by using the
			grammar pattern 'ka dou ka.' Adding this pattern to the end of a
			sentence turns it into an embedded question that can then be used
			inside a larger sentence. The diagram shows the details of the
			sentence to use as the embedded question along with English text
			showing the form that the answer should take.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The English text in the diagram shows the
			basic form that the answer should take. The
			diagram indicates that the subject (S) is
			orange juice, further identified by the demonstrative (D) "this." The
			adjective (Aj) describing the orange juice is delicious.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
</lesson>

		<answerJ サリー さん は ジョン さん に ワイン を あげます>
		<answerK サリー さん は ジョン さん に ワイン を あげます>
		<questionType Question Type - Giving>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Giving
				<off>Receiving
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we are required to create a statement about someone giving
			something to another person, and that it should be in the present form. 
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			The questions in this lesson all involve giving and receiving of objects.  
			This type of question places the focus on the giver.
			Be careful when either the giver or the receiver is a member of your family (or yourself), as
			you may need to change the verb.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The action i.e. the verb (V) is "to give,"
			and the subject (S) who is giving is Sally.
			The person (P) receiving is John. 
			The direct object (O) of the verb is some wine.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>

				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>

			something to another person, and that it should be a question in the past form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			The questions in this lesson all involve giving and receiving of an object or action.  
			The focus is on the receiver in this type of question.
			Be careful when either the giver or the receiver is a member of your family (or yourself), as
			you may need to change the verb.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>

			the person (S) receiving is Tarou. 
			The person (P) giving is his older sister. 
			The direct object (O) of the verb is a box.  
		</diagHelp>

		<sentence I said that I play video games>
		<answerJ ゲーム を する と いった>
		<answerK ゲーム を する と 言った>
		<questionType Question Type - Quotations>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Quotation
				<off>Description
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Non-Past
				<on>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows that you must make a
			quotation stating that an action would be performed, and that it should be in the plain past form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this lesson, you are asked to use a
			quotation to describe what was said. This is not a direct quote, but
			an interpreted quote that summarizes what was said without repeating
			the exact words. The left side of the diagram shows what to quote, including a verb and
			details such as the subject. The right side of the diagram shows the verb to use to indicate the quote.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The action on the left side of the diagram
			shows that the action is described by the verb (V) "to do" and its
			direct object (O), video games. The right side shows the verb (V)
			"to say" to indicate that we must create a quotation.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson25_2.png>
		<sentence I think that he will come tomorrow>
		<answerJ あした くる と おもいます>
		<answerK 明日 来る と 思います>
		<questionType Question Type - Quotations>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Quotation
				<off>Description
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form indicates that you must
			express what someone is thinking, and that your answer should be a positive statement in the
			non-past polite form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this lesson, you will practise how to say
			what someone is thinking by using a subordinate clause followed by
			in English. The diagram indicates the action in the subordinate
			clause, including the verb and possibly details such as the subject.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The action is described by the verb (V) "to come" and the time (T) tomorrow.
			You must use the verb (V) "to think" to express this action.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

		<diagram Examples/lesson25_3.png>
		<sentence A person called Sam>
		<answerJ サム と いう ひと>
		<answerK サム と 言う 人>
		<questionType Question Type - Description>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Quotation
				<on>Description
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form indicates that you must
			create a description, which should be a positive statement in the
			non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this lesson, you will practise using the
			phrase 'to iu' to give a description. This grammar pattern indicates
			that the thing being described is a specific instance of a general
			category of things. The diagram shows both the object to describe and
			the description to use.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The object (O) to describe is Sam. You must use
			the verb (V) "to say" to describe him as a (O) human being.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
</lesson>

	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson26_1.png>
		<sentence Even though he was busy, Sam took a nap>
		<answerJ サム は いそがしい のに ひるね した>
		<answerK サムは 忙しい のに 昼寝 した>
		<questionType Question Type - Unexpected Outcomes>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>"のに"
				<off>"ても"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Non-Past
				<on>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that we must use 'Noni' in the answer to express a contradiction,
			and that the answer should be a statement in in the past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			For this type of question, you must connect
			two sentences together with 'no ni,' which implies that the action
			described in the second sentence is not what you expected from the
			information given in the first. The top half of the diagram shows the
			information and the bottom half shows the unexpected results. All displayed information
			should be given in your answer, and extra information should not be included.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The top half of the diagram shows that the
			subject (S) Sam is described by the adjective (Aj) busy. The bottom
			half shows the unexpected result, described by the verb (V) "to do" and the
			direct object (O) napping.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson26_2.png>
		<sentence It's a waste of time to ask Sally about Mathematics>
		<answerJ サリーに すうがくに ついて きいても むだだ>
		<answerK サリーに 数学に ついて 聞いても 無駄だ>
		<questionType Question Type - Expressing "Even if">
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<off>"のに"
				<on>"ても"
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Polite
				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that the answer must
			express that an outcome holds even if the condition given in another
			is true, and that it should be a positive statement in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question you will practise
			sentences which express that one sentence is true even if the
			condition given in another is true. You will use the 'te'
			form of a verb or adjective followed by 'mo,' which together carry
			the nuance that "even if" does in English. The top half of the
			diagram shows the sentence that is the condition, and the bottom half
			gives the sentence holds true if that condition is true.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The top half of the diagram gives the condition, where the verb (V) is "asking" Sally about the object (O)
			Mathematics. The bottom half shows the second sentence, which is
			an adjective (Aj) indicating that it is a waste.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
</lesson>

			the polite past form.

			In this type of question, you will practise a
			grammar pattern that is used to indicate a volitional decision to
			perform an action. The left half of the diagram shows the action that will be
			performed, including which verb is used and details such as the
			direct object. The right half of the diagram gives a reminder of the verb, 'suru,' which is used in this grammar pattern.
		</gfxHelp>

			described by the verb (V) "to buy" and the direct object (O)
			coffee. The right half of the diagram shows the verb (V) "to do,"
			which is used in the grammar pattern.

				<on>Past

				<on>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>

			The grammar form shows us that we must
			describe an action that is performed irregardless of the speaker's
			volition. The answer should be in the non-past plain form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			For this type of question, you must indicate
			that an action is performed irregardless of your volition. This
			grammar pattern is usually used to describe that the decision to
			carry out the action was made by an unspecified agent, but it may
			simply indicate unintentional results. The left half of the
			diagram shows the action performed, and the right half gives a
			reminder of the verb used in this grammar pattern.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The left half of the diagram shows the action, described by the
			verb (V) "to do" and the direct object (O), a fight. The right half of the
			diagram shows the verb (V) "to become," which is used in the grammar pattern.
		</diagHelp>

<lesson>
	<title 'She surprised me' - Introduction to the causative form>
	<id 28>
	<level 3>
	<question compulsion 1.0>
		<concept causative1 1.0>
			<grammar CAUSATIVE1>
			<diagram diagram1>
		</concept>
	</question>
	<question permission 1.0>
		<concept causative1 1.0>
			<grammar CAUSATIVE1>
			<diagram diagram2>
		</concept>
	</question>
	<question request 1.0>
		<concept causative1 1.0>
			<grammar CAUSATIVE2>
			<diagram diagram3>
		</concept>
	</question>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Compulsion>
			question == compulsion
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Permission>
			question == permission
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Request>
			question == request
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Statement>
			type == statement
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Question>
			type == question
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>
	<formgroup>
		<form_desc Non-Past>
			tense == present 
		</form_desc>
		<form_desc Past>
			tense == past
		</form_desc>
	</formgroup>
	<diagram diagram1>		
		<gfxgroup center>
			<gfx label>
				<text Outline:>
				<coords 25 0 400 26>
				<restriction {verbForm} type == question>
					<appendS Is [Who] compelled to [Verb]?>
				</restriction>
				<restriction {verbForm} type == statement>
					<appendS [Who] is compelled to [Verb]>
				</restriction>
				<restriction {verbForm} tense == past>
					<subS is was>
				</restriction>
				<restriction {verbForm} tense == past>
					<subS Is Was>
				</restriction>					
			</gfx>
		</gfxgroup>
		<gfxgroup center>
			<gfx with> 
				<gfx_data [Subject]>			
				<coords 150 90 125 125>	
				<gfx_marker Misc/subject.gif>	
				<gfx_marker_text Who caused the action>
			</gfx>
			<gfx place> 
				<gfx_data [Who]>			
				<coords 290 90 125 125>	
				<gfx_marker Misc/place.gif>
				<gfx_marker_text Who did the action>
			</gfx>
		</gfxgroup>
		<gfxgroup center>
			<gfx object> 
				<gfx_data [What]>			
				<coords 75 230 140 140>	
				<gfx_marker Misc/object.gif>
				<gfx_marker_text This is the object>
			</gfx>
			<gfx place> 
				<gfx_data [Destination]>			
				<coords 75 230 140 140>	
				<gfx_marker Misc/place.gif>
				<gfx_marker_text This is the destination>
			</gfx>
			<gfx verb> 
				<gfx_data [Verb]>			
				<coords 235 230 140 140>	
				<gfx_marker Misc/verb.gif>
				<gfx_marker_text This is the verb>
			</gfx>
			<gfx negative> 
				<restriction {verbForm} sign == negative>
					<text negative>
					<coords 350 325 50 50>
					<image Misc/negative.gif>				
				</restriction>
			</gfx>
			<gfx question> 
				<restriction {verbForm} type == question>
					<text question>
					<coords 350 325 50 50>

			The grammar form shows us that we are required to create a sentence regarding
			someone being compelled to do something, and that the sentence should be in the
			form of a question. It should also be created using the past tense.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			The questions in this lesson all involve using the causative verb form. In this example,
			the causative form is used to express the meaning of compulsion - i.e. someone being
			compelled to perform an action of some sort. The diagram shows the person doing the
			action (P), the object involved in the action (O), and the action itself (V). In other cases,
			the person doing the compelling may be shown (S).
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The person (P) compelled to do the action is Taro. 
			The object (O) of the suggested action is a letter.  
			The action itself, i.e. the verb (V) is "to write."
			An outline of the desired answer is also given in English.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

			positive statement in the plain past form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			This type of question requires you to create a
			sentence which uses the causative passive form of a verb. This
			construct expresses that someone was forced to do something, and
			carries the nuance that they did not enjoy it. It may also show the
			speaker's concern for the subject who was forced to do the
			action. As in other types of sentences the
			subject (for example, "I") may be omitted if understood from
			context, so the diagram does not necessarily
			show the subject or actor. 
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>

			by the verb (V) "to be forced to buy" and its
			direct object (O), a vase. Both the subject and actor are omitted.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>

				<gfx_marker_text This is the verb>
			</gfx>
			<gfx Verb1-neg>
				<restriction {form3} sign == negative>
					<text negative>
					<coords 360 320 40 40>
					<image Misc/negative.gif>
				</restriction>
			</gfx>
		</gfxgroup>
	</diagram>

	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson30_1.png>
		<sentence I said "I will go tomorrow.">
		<answerJ あす いきます と もうしあげました>
		<answerK 明日 行きます と 申し上げました>
		<questionType Question Type - Irregular Verbs>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Keigo
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<off>Non-Past
				<on>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Polite
				<off>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that the answer must
			be a positive statement in the polite past form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question, you will practise
			using irregular humble and honorific verbs.
			The diagram shows the action to express, including the verb and
			details such as the direct object or place where the action is performed.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The bottom half of the diagram shows that the
			humble form of the verb (V) "to say" will be used to describe the action in the top
			half. This action is described by the verb (V) "to go" and the time
			(T) tomorrow.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson30_2.png>
		<sentence Someone will come to the museum>
		<answerJ びじゅつかん に おいでになる>
		<answerK 美術館 に おいでになる>
		<questionType Question Type - come/go/be (honorific)>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Keigo
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Polite
				<off>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that the answer must
			be a positive statement in the polite present form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			In this type of question, you will practise
			using the honorific forms of verbs. These
			forms are used when the person performing the action is a superior or
			has higher social status than the speaker. The diagram shows the action that
			you must express with the honorific form, including the verb and
			details such as the direct object.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The diagram shows that the action is described
			by the honorific form of the verb (V) "to come/go/be" and that the
			destination (O) is the museum.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
	<example>
		<diagram Examples/lesson30_3.png>
		<sentence I will send a letter>
		<answerJ てがみ を おおくりする>
		<answerK 手紙 を お送りする>
		<questionType Question Type - Humble Forms>
		<form>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Keigo
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Statement
				<off>Question
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Positive
				<off>Negative
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Non-Past
				<off>Past
			</fgroup>
			<fgroup>
				<on>Polite
				<off>Plain
			</fgroup>
		</form>
		<formHelp>
			The grammar form shows us that the answer must
			be a positive statement in the polite present form.
		</formHelp>
		<gfxHelp>
			For this type of question, you are asked to
			describe a actions using the humble (or modest) forms of verbs. These forms are
			used when speaking to a superior about the your own actions (or those
			of your peers). The diagram shows the action to describe, including
			the verb and details such as the time when the action is performed.
		</gfxHelp>
		<diagHelp>
			The diagram shows that the verb (V) is the
			humble/modest form of "to send" and that the direct object (O) is a letter.
		</diagHelp>
	</example>
